Calls the `Create()` method on a `rest.Creater` implementation\\n\\nFor Deployments, the Creater is the `REST` struct defined in `pkg/registry/apps/deployment/storage/storage.go`. This REST storage implementation wraps `genericregistry.Store` and applies Deployment-specific validation strategies. The Store ultimately calls through to the etcd3 storage backend via `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/etcd3/store.go`, where the `store.Create()` function serializes the Deployment object (typically as JSON or protobuf) and prepares it for persistence.\\n\\n**STORAGE LAYER (etcd-io-etcd):**\\nThe serialized Deployment is passed to etcd's key-value store implementation. The etcd3 backend interfaces with the MVCC (Multi-Version Concurrency Control) engine defined in `server/mvcc/kvstore.go`. A write transaction is created (implementing the `TxnWrite` interface from `server/mvcc/kv.go`), and the serialized Deployment is written to the key-value store via the `Put()` method defined in the `WriteView` interface. \\n\\nThe `Put()` method in `server/mvcc/kvstore.go` performs the actual write operation, allocating a new revision number, updating the in-memory index, and persisting the key-value pair to the underlying BoltDB backend. The transaction is then committed, making the Deployment object durable and visible to all future read operations.\\n\\n**Summary:**\\nThe complete flow is: client application → kubernetes-client-go REST Client → API server HTTP handler → DeploymentInterface.Create() → REST storage Create() → etcd3 store.Create() → etcd MVCC store Put() → persistent storage (BoltDB). Each layer adds validation, transformation, and durability guarantees, ensuring that the Deployment specification is accurately stored and can be retrieved by controllers and other clients.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
